# Introduction {.heading_70}

These four very brief letters are found in the collection of "epistles" which came to be labeled as the ["General Epistles"]{.class_2223} or ["Catholic Epistles."]{.class_2223} The entire set is Hebrews--Revelation: nine epistles. The two titles given to them are misleading and dangerous. The truth is, there is nothing "Catholic" about [Hebrews]{.class_2223} or [Revelation]{.class_2223} at all, and [James]{.class_2223} is addressed to no one but the ["twelve tribes"]{.class_2226} of Israel (James 1:1). In Kenneth Taylor's dead "bible"---commonly miscalled [The Living Bible]{.class_2223}---James 1:1 had to be altered to fit the ignorance and perverseness of its revisor (Kenneth Taylor). He forced James to say that the epistle was written to Christian Jews. It certainly was [not;]{.class_2223} at least not in any copy of any manuscript in Latin, Syrian, Greek, Gothic, Coptic, English, French, Spanish, Russian, Italian, or German that has ever been found by anyone in [nineteen centuries.]{.class_2223}

Taylor's rotten revision is exactly like that of his contemporaries: Palmer, Farstad, Harris, Bob Jones III, Fee, Phillips, Walker, Foster, Youngblood, Linton, Kenneth Wuest, Spiros Zodhiates, A. T. Robertson, Nida, Aland, Metzger, et al.

Exactly as [Matthew]{.class_2223} and [Acts]{.class_2223} are "transitional books," so [Hebrews]{.class_2223} joins them to take you into times that will take place AFTER the Body of Christ has been called home to the Judgment Seat of Christ and the Marriage of the Lamb. ## Chapter 4 {.heading_371}

4:1 Beloved, believe not every spirit, but try the spirits whether they are of God: because many false prophets are gone out into the world.

2 Hereby know ye the Spirit of God: Every spirit that confesseth that Jesus Christ is come in the flesh is of God:

3 And every spirit that confesseth not that Jesus Christ is come in the flesh is not of God: and this is that spirit of antichrist, whereof ye have heard that it should come; and even now already is it in the world.

4 Ye are of God, little children, and have overcome them: because greater is he that is in you, than he that is in the world.

5 They are of the world: therefore speak they of the world, and the world heareth them.

6 We are of God: he that knoweth God heareth us; he that is not of God heareth not us. Hereby know we the spirit of truth, and the spirit of error.

Now for a little while, at least, we have some "friendly skies" in which to fly. There is little in these six verses that cannot be applied to a Christian in this age [or]{.class_2223} the Tribulation. To start with, you should discern that the[ "spirits"]{.class_2226} mentioned are connected with PEOPLE: ["try the spirits\...because many false PROPHETS are gone out into the world]{.class_2226} (vs. 1).

Although that seems incidental, it is not incidental when the false prophet of Revelation 13:11--15 shows up; for when you put him into a "trinity" which would include a false [father,]{.class_2223} false [son,]{.class_2223} and false holy spirit it will come out at ["BAAL"]{.class_2226}---a false god the Father, ["BALAK"]{.class_2226}---a false god the son, and ["BALAAM"]{.class_2226}---a false god the holy spirit (see Num. 22--23; 1 Kings 18; 2 Kings 10).

The false holy spirit, [there,]{.class_2223} is a PROPHET (Rev. 13:11).

Now there are [three spirits]{.class_2223} that can come out of a man's mouth when he speaks. Job would ask you ["whose SPIRIT came from thee?"]{.class_2226} (Job 26:2--4) when you tried to ["plentifully declare the thing"]{.class_2226} as it was. ["Spirit"]{.class_2226} is ["wind"]{.class_2226}[]{#ayjLIa8nTIWM3oX9-kjcSw905.xhtml_page_101} (see John 3:8; Ezek. 37:9,14; Gen. 2:7; Job 32:8).

This means that there is a spiritual "exchange" going on when any preacher of the Bible stands up and delivers his message[ in the power of the Holy Spirit]{.class_2223} (see 1 Cor. 2:1, 4). There is a sense in which he actually "ministers" [the Holy Spirit]{.class_2223} to the listener---[without]{.class_2223} any "laying on of hands."

Years ago, when all of my sons were young (1970--1990), they used to kid me about my enthusiasm for hearing men [preach:]{.class_2223} like Lester Roloff, Hugh Pyle, and Bob Gray. They said, "Dad, what if someone gave you a free ticket to the Superbowl and the same day Bob Gray was speaking in a Bible conference. Wouldn't you go to the game then?" "No," I said, "I'd rather hear Bob Gray." "But Daaad! What if the Superbowl was right here where[ you lived;]{.class_2223} say five or ten miles from here?" "I'd go hear Bob Gray," I said. And I meant it.

My sons never did really believe me, I don't guess, but I meant every word I said. You see, there is something that "takes place" in a church service where the preacher believes the Book and is "confessed up" and "prayed up" before he comes into the pulpit. Whether you call this ["unction"]{.class_2226} (see 1 John 2:20) or an ["anointing"]{.class_2226} (1 John 2:27), the [results]{.class_2223} are the same; there is a definite spiritual "transaction" that takes place [between ]{.class_2223}the preacher's mouth and the hearer's ears (see Matt. 13:9; Luke 8:8; Mark 4:23; Rev. 3:6, 13, 22).

You know, I used to hate it when a mob would mob me at the end of a preaching service (1952--1992) where no one had gotten saved. They all lined up to shake my hand and get my autograph while saying, "Boy, I got a BLESSING out of that message tonight!" or "I sure got a blessing tonight," or "Brother Ruckman, that message BLESSED my soul!" I would grit my teeth, nod my head, and mumble (silently to myself): "Yeah? Well, what are you going to do about it?" I was bitter because I never intended to be a movie star or object of[ anyone's]{.class_2223} admiration or adoration; [I wanted to see grown men SAVED.]{.class_2223}

Well, I got to thinking, "What is a 'blessing'?"

I wasn't getting any "blessing." Half the time the people weren't praying, the offering wasn't enough to get me through the next week, []{#ayjLIa8nTIWM3oX9-kjcSw905.xhtml_page_102}I was having "wife troubles" during the meeting, but even worse, no one was getting saved. In the tidal wave of people who nearly smothered me at the end of the service, I often lost some of my chalk or my sermon notes or my glasses or my pens and (sometimes) my Bible.

To say I was "irritated" was to put it mildly. Then one day the Lord showed me something. About forty-two years ago, I was going through some pretty "rough stuff." At that time, I was visiting a little country church where a Methodist preacher (Fritz Folsom) was preaching. He was an old-time, [saved ]{.class_2223}Methodist preacher and a Bible believer (believe it or not!). That preacher had just taken his wife to the hospital to have their fifth baby.

Well, she gave birth to the baby; it was a baby boy, in good health. The preacher and his four other children---along with some friends and relatives---were down in the waiting room, so naturally they were all [rejoicing]{.class_2223} and praising God for the answer to their prayers.

Right in the middle of this [rejoicing,]{.class_2223} word came from upstairs that someone had given the mother the wrong blood in a transfusion that had been necessary shortly after the birth. It was the wrong kind of blood, and the mother was [dead:]{.class_2223} dead within thirty minutes after the baby was born. That left the preacher to act as "momma" for [five young children]{.class_2223}---the oldest being about sixteen.

The night I heard him preach was two weeks after that disaster. He peached on "living by faith" and "having faith in God."

When he got through there wasn't a dry eye in that room. And, man, I had gone into that "service" as limp as a dishrag, but I came out of it like a roaring lion!

But when I got up out of my seat I found myself saying to myself, "Boy, go up there and tell that bird what a BLESSING you got from his message!" I sat down hard on [that ]{.class_2223}one! It was right there that the Lord stopped me and said, "Hey there! What are you doing, buddy? I thought you didn't believe in people shaking a preacher's hand and telling him about what a blessing they had received from his message? Are you a hypocrite or what?"

I hesitated to get up. I had to do some hard thinking. "What is it I am doing? Why did I think of doing what I condemned in others? I know something has [happened]{.class_2223}[]{#ayjLIa8nTIWM3oX9-kjcSw905.xhtml_page_103} here, but I cannot explain what it is!"

I know NOW what "it is." When a preacher is "prayed up" and believes that Book and gets up and preaches it without fear or favor (as it is written), [something more happens than just "talk."]{.class_2223} A [spiritual transaction]{.class_2223} takes place in that assembly, wherever it is. The speaker is "ministering the Spirit." The Holy Spirit is speaking THROUGH HIM (see 2 Pet. 1:21).

# The General Epistle of 2 John {.heading_1420}

## Introduction {#ayjLIa8nTIWM3oX9-kjcSw1414.xhtml_ayjLIa8nTIWM3oX9-kjcSw2215 .heading_1422}

This very short epistle is one verse shorter than 3 John. As such, it is shorter than [Obadiah]{.class_2223} in the Old Tesatment and [Philemon]{.class_2223} in the New Testament. Although it is one verse shorter than [3 John,]{.class_2223} it has more words in it (303 vs. 299). There is no way that anyone can date these epistles "for sure," but most commentators guess somewhere around A.D. 80--85. The oldest "dated" scrap of paper we have of Scripture (about A.D. 120) is a fragment called "P52"; it contains a very tiny part of less than a half page on which John 18 was written.

The reason why no one can reach back to an "original" and pick it up is easy to explain if you know anything about Bible believers; it is also true that if you know anything about Bible-believing Christians you can understand why the most corrupt and [unreliable]{.class_2223} Greek manuscripts ([א]{.class_2236}, B, D, etc.) will be the ones in the BEST CONDITION.

This truth, quite naturally, is hidden from Alexandrian apostates like A. T. Robertson, James White, J. P. Free, Earl Kalland, Kenneth Wuest, Westcott, Hort, Aland, Metzger, Tischendorf, Lachmann, Griesbach, Eugene Nida, Alan McRae, Arthur Farstad, Woodrow Kroll, and Robert Sumner.

Consequently, in dealing with any set of Bible manuscripts or [any]{.class_2223} version of [any]{.class_2223} translation, they never really value it enough to spend hours with it, [believing]{.class_2223} it. They all use some "Bible" [to make a living,]{.class_2223} and that is the total heighth and depth of their spiritual life. Not one of them "stands in AWE" of what he is reading (Psa. 19:18, 120). 1:1 The elder unto the elect lady and her children, whom I love in the truth; and not I only, but also all they that have known the truth;

# The General Epistle of Jude {.heading_70}

## Introduction {#ayjLIa8nTIWM3oX9-kjcSw1621.xhtml_ayjLIa8nTIWM3oX9-kjcSw2220 .heading_1422}

The General Epistle of Jude has one chapter, like Philemon, 2 and 3 John, and Obadiah. It has twenty-five verses and 613 words.

The apostolic authorship of the book has been removed by the Scholars' Union (Alexandrian apostates) on the grounds the apostle (["Judas, the brother of James"]{.class_2226}---not Judas Iscariot, Luke 6:16) couldn't have written verse 17. This would produce a "father and son" among the twelve disciples as Judas (not "Iscariot") would have ["James the SON of Alphaeus"]{.class_2226} (Luke 6:15) for his FATHER!

This type of fruitless attacks on the [AV]{.class_2223} text shows you the "mind set" of [The Greek Expositor's New Testament,]{.class_2223} and all publications like it from every Greek scholar connected with any revision of the [King James Bible]{.class_2223} since the days of Westcott and Hort (1870--1890).

You see, every Greek manuscript "extant," on Jude 1:1, says that the ["Jude"]{.class_2226} there (the author of the book) was the ["brother of James"]{.class_2226}---not the "son."
